        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781842555040" href="/book/show/889503.I_Coriander">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5121297-alison?shelf=confident-readers-chapter-books">confident-readers-chapter-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer312956223&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer312956223" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4225589976772181081">This is a wonderful fairy tale novel. Coriander, growing up in the era of Cromwell's protectorate after the Royalist defeat in the Civil War, is the daughter of a wealthy merchant. Her mother is well known as a herbalist and healer, and, Coriander learns, is from Fairyland.<br/><br/>Coriander's mother dies, and since rumours are abounding of his sympathies, her father is advised to marry a good Puritan woman. So Coriander acquires a wicked stepmother in Maud, and a cowed, frightened stepsister in Hester. </span>
  <span id="freeText4225589976772181081" style="display:none">This is a wonderful fairy tale novel. Coriander, growing up in the era of Cromwell's protectorate after the Royalist defeat in the Civil War, is the daughter of a wealthy merchant. Her mother is well known as a herbalist and healer, and, Coriander learns, is from Fairyland.<br /><br />Coriander's mother dies, and since rumours are abounding of his sympathies, her father is advised to marry a good Puritan woman. So Coriander acquires a wicked stepmother in Maud, and a cowed, frightened stepsister in Hester. Then Maud brings Arise Fell, a Puritan preacher, into the house, and Coriander's world is shattered. She journeys to Fairyland, and there learns that she has the courage and intelligence to defeat evil both there and in the real world.<br /><br />I loved this book. It works for me as a fairy tale: there is a wicked fairy queen, a handsome though enchanted prince, a princess who is not aware that she is a princess, even a magic mirror. <br /><br />Other reviewers have complained about the historical accuracy, that witches were less persecuted under the Puritans than under James 1, which is probably true- but firstly, think about Salem witch trials- the inhabitants were most definitely Puritans- and secondly, Maud and Arise are not Puritans, they are *spoiler* false prophets and opportunists of the worst kind. Highly recommended for confident readers, 8+.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4225589976772181081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_66752525" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Susann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/959531-susann"><img alt="Susann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1204475578p2/959531.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_2360361802" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2360361802" />
    <a title="Whitney Collins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12554473-whitney-collins"><img alt="Whitney Collins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428006334p2/12554473.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2360361802?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Collins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Collins" href="/user/show/12554473-whitney-collins">Whitney Collins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2360361802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7846008234395917902">Every so often, I get a hankering for a good young adult novel. This one scratched that itch, and definitely took me back to my childhood. It is a beautiful fairy tale, reminiscent of Ella Enchanted (my all time favorite book as a child). The prose has a beautiful, ethereal quality, and I think it could be a enjoyable read for adults and young-adults alike. <br/><br/>No matter what your age, every so often, we need to escape the mundane of our ordinary lives and add in a little magic. This book does the t</span>
  <span id="freeText7846008234395917902" style="display:none">Every so often, I get a hankering for a good young adult novel. This one scratched that itch, and definitely took me back to my childhood. It is a beautiful fairy tale, reminiscent of Ella Enchanted (my all time favorite book as a child). The prose has a beautiful, ethereal quality, and I think it could be a enjoyable read for adults and young-adults alike. <br /><br />No matter what your age, every so often, we need to escape the mundane of our ordinary lives and add in a little magic. This book does the trick. It is a quintessential fairy tale with a little historical fiction thrown in. There is a young girl whose beautiful mother dies tragically young. Her father quickly remarries to avoid scrutiny from the Puritans in control of England at the time, but her new stepmother is wicked to say the least. The stereotypical mold is broken in a few ways: her stepsister being a kind hearted friend one of them. <br /><br />We get plenty of fairies, magic, travel between worlds, and wickedness. It made me feel like a kid again; there is just something special about the magic of fairy tales that never grows old, no matter what your age. Coriander was a strong character, keeping her kind heart and drive no matter what life threw at her. There are some extremely dark things that occur, but I still think it was appropriate for young readers, especially considering how Coriander handled those things. <br /><br />We flip between two worlds-the magical fairy world Coriander's mother was from, and the Puritan controlled England of the 1600s. Gardner did an excellent job combining the two, and making the evil Coriander suffers seem believable. The misinformed religious characters really were terrifying, and how they twisted the Bible to meet their own desires is unfortunately something that happened far too often (and still does). Many of the things they claimed were the exact opposite of what Jesus taught, and as Coriander said, Maud and Arise were the true devils. <br /><br />The few things that bothered me were the way Coriander and Tycho quickly and inexplicably fell in love. I would have liked to see a bit more character development there. The time difference between worlds was also never fully explained, and there were a bit too many minor characters thrown in that seemed to have no point. Overall, however, this was a great escape into a land of fairies, wicked stepmothers, and magic, and definitely made me feel young again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7846008234395917902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17705397512030664644">„I have been thinking that written words are mighty powerful, more so than talking and telling.“ <br/><br/>And you would be right, Hester. <br/><br/>I don‘t even know where to begin with, as this book hit me like a train. I felt it calling to me from the library shelf and it would not stop pestering me until I picked and opened it up. Mighty mistake, for it has attached itself to my heart and I highly doubt it will ever let me go.<br/><br/>The closest thing I can relate my reading experience to, is watching Spirited Away for</span>
  <span id="freeText17705397512030664644" style="display:none">„I have been thinking that written words are mighty powerful, more so than talking and telling.“ <br /><br />And you would be right, Hester. <br /><br />I don‘t even know where to begin with, as this book hit me like a train. I felt it calling to me from the library shelf and it would not stop pestering me until I picked and opened it up. Mighty mistake, for it has attached itself to my heart and I highly doubt it will ever let me go.<br /><br />The closest thing I can relate my reading experience to, is watching Spirited Away for the first time and even that is an understatement. <br /><br />This book is basically a fairytale, a story about growing up, about fighting injustice, about the evil that disguises itself as God, about actual God-loving humans, about family, about grief, about fantastical worlds and our own. All of this wrapped up in a girl‘s tale, Coriander, someone I felt so connected to that I might even believe her to have whispered her journey to me.<br /><br />I read this novel in one sitting and, much like Coriander every time she took of her silver shoes, afterwards I felt abruptly out of place. Like I am waiting to go back to these characters.<br /><br />How wonderful it is to be able to read stories that make you feel like this ❤️</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Y7NtUhyXoftsikeWA2SBpWRQsyQ7qaGnpUSxc+8omp0cYYpzRTORkzi4fflnDRsc7bPCw0Ea3f/19wXyGTTRJQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dZrO39kHs03BtOyqliOjv6vt8j6hs+SG8fE7kvDIO08KSCn+gKODJZWG1sXySjkGIg6D2dsAmN6hQo8TBtRw9w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11458839937429969703">Sally Gardner grew up and still lives in London. Being dyslexic, she did not learn to read or write until she was fourteen and had been thrown out of several schools, labeled unteachable, and sent to a school for maladjusted children. Despite this, she gained a degree with highest honors at a leading London art college, followed by a scholarship to a theater school, and then went on to become a ve</span>
  <span id="freeText11458839937429969703" style="display:none">Sally Gardner grew up and still lives in London. Being dyslexic, she did not learn to read or write until she was fourteen and had been thrown out of several schools, labeled unteachable, and sent to a school for maladjusted children. Despite this, she gained a degree with highest honors at a leading London art college, followed by a scholarship to a theater school, and then went on to become a very successful costume designer, working on some notable productions. <br /><br />After the births of twin daughters and a son, she started first to illustrate and then to write picture books and chapter books, usually with fairytale- or otherwise magical subject matter. She has been called 'an idiosyncratic genius' by London’s Sunday Times.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11458839937429969703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
